рд╕реНрддреБрд╖реЗ рдЬрдирдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдардВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рднрд╛рд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬрд╕реНрдп рдЛрдЬрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рди рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ред рдЕрдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╖рдЯреНрдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╛рд╢рджрдХреНрд╖рд░рд╛ рд╢рдХреНрдХрд░реА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ — рд╕реНрддреБрд╖реЗ рдкрдЪреНрдЪреЛрди рдЛрдЬрд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рд╣ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдВ рд╣ рд╢рдХреНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдиреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реНрдпреВрд│реНрд╣реЗ рджрд╢рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореЗрд╜рд╣рдиреАрджрдВ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдирд┐рд╡рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдирдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ - рдЛрднреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рднреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕реНрддреБрд╖реЗ рдЬрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╡реИрд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдореН ’ (рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рео. рео) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЖрджреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╣рд╛рдирд╛рдореНрдиреАрд╡реНрд░рддреЗ рдЬрдкреНрдпрд╛ рее

Jamison Brereton

49 (490)
All Gods
R╠еji┼Ыvan Bh─Бradv─Бja
15 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except ┼Ыakvar─л 15
A hymn of straightforward structure, typical of many All God hymns: each verse praises a single god (or divine entity, like the pair Night and Dawn [vs. 3] or the group of Maruts [vs. 11]). Most verses name the god in question, though the name can be postponed till late in the verse, as in verse 2 dedicated to Agni or verse 8 to P┼лс╣гan, whose name is the last word in the verse. Two do not name the god at all: verse 3 to Night and Dawn and verse 12 to Indra. The riddling tech
nique of postponing or omitting the name of an entity defined by the verse is of course common in R╠еgvedic rhetoric, and its use in All God catalogues is especially appropriate.
There is no obvious ritual or other significance to the order of gods in this hymn, though many of the parties to the Morning Pressing occur early in the hymn: Agni (vs. 2), Night and Dawn (vs. 3), V─Бyu (vs. 4), A┼Ыvins (vs. 5). On the other hand, the verse dedicated to Indra (12), a regular participant in the dawn ritual, is late in the hymn, though he is obliquely present, with the Maruts, in 6cd. No god receives more than a single verse, though, as just mentioned, Indra and the Maruts have a presence in the Parjanya and V─Бta [=Thunder and Wind] verse (6), as Agni does

in the Mitra and Varuс╣Зa verse (1) and in the Tvaс╣гс╣нar verse (9). The reference shifts between the 3rd and 2nd person, with the former predominating. The final verse of the hymn, in a slightly different meter (triс╣гс╣нubh but with an extra p─Бda), mentions no specific gods, but asks all of them for benefits.

Jamison Brereton Notes

All Gods The verb тАШquicken, enlivenтАЩ (тИЪjinv) appears at widely scattered intervals in this hymn (6b jinvatam, 11c j├нnvath─Б, 14d jinvatu), but enough to count as a leitmotif.

рд╕реБрд╡реНрд░рддрдВ рд╕реБрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрдВ рдЬрдирдВ рджреИрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдЬрдирдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╕рдВрдШ рдирд╡реНрдпрд╕реАрднрд┐рдГ рдирд╡рддрд░рд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЧреАрд░реНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрд╖реЗ рдЕрд╣рдВ рд╕реНрддреБрд╡реЗ ред рддрдерд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛ ред рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ рдкреНрд░рдореАрддреЗрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдпрдХреЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ рдкрд╛рдкрдиреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╛ред рдПрддрд╛рд╡рдкрд┐ рджреЗрд╡реМ рд╕реНрддреМрдорд┐ ред рдХреАрджреГрд╢реМ ред рд╕реБрдореНрдирдпрдиреНрддрд╛ рд╕реБрдореНрдирдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреДрдгрд╛рдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреМ ред рд╕реБрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдмрд▓рд╛рдГ рддреЗ рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛рджрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЗрд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рдЖ рдЧрдордиреНрддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреБ ред рддреЗ рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рдГ рд╢реНрд░реБрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреАрдГ рд╢реГрдгреНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рдЪ ред рдЕрддреНрд░ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдЧрдгрдирдореБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдХрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреНред рдЕрдд рдПрд╡ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдВ рдЬрдирдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдиреНрдпрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI commend with new hymns the man observant of his duty, and the beneficent Mitra and Varuс╣Зa; may they, the mighty ones, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, and Agni, come to our rite, and listen (to our praises).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The man observant: stuс╣гe janam suvratam = daivyam janam, the divine people, devasaс╣Еgham, the company of the gods

Jamison Brereton

I will praise the people of good commandment with newer hymns, will praise Mitra and Varuс╣Зa the gracious.
Let them come hither; let them listen hereтАФthose of good dominion, Varuс╣Зa, Mitra, Agni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although non-formulaic groupings of gods are frequently encountered in All God hymns, the trio v├бruс╣Зo mitr├│ agn├нс╕е is perhaps a little strange, since we expect this trioтАЩs third member to be instead Aryaman. And indeed that sequence is quite common: there is a much-repeated dimeter p─Бda v├бruс╣Зo mitr├│ aryam─Б╠Б(I.26.4, etc.; see repetitions listed in Lubotsky), and the same sequence is regularly found at the end of a Jagat─л p─Бda (I.40.5, V.46.5, VII.66.11, 12, etc.). I wonder if agn├нс╕е is some sort of makeshift substitute for aryam─Б╠Бin a Triс╣гс╣нubh cadence where aryam─Б╠БwouldnтАЩt fit (cf. the same sequence in the acc. in the next hymn, VI.50.1, and it is found elsewhere in both nom. and acc., incl. the repeated p─Бda VI.51.10). After all, Agni is compatible with pretty much any Vedic god and could be slotted in when the more specialized divinity was metrically inconvenient.

Griffith

I LAUD with newest songs the Righteous People, Mitra and Varuna who make us happy.
Let them approach, here let them listen,Agni, Varuna, Mitra, Lords of fair dominion.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(I incite the worshipper) to offer worship to Agni, who is to be adored at the sacrifices of every ma; whose acts are free from arrogance; the lord of the two youthful (brides, heaven and earth); the child of heaven, the son of strength, the briliant symbol of sacrifice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The one to be reverently invoked at the ceremonies of every clan, of undistracted resolve, the spoked wheel of the two youthful ones
[=Heaven and Earth],
the child of Heaven, the son of strengthтАФAgniтАФthe ruddy beacon of the sacrifice (I invoke) to perform sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The fuller expression in X.3.7 div├бspr╠еthivy├│r arat├нr yuvaty├│с╕е тАЬthe spoked wheel of Heaven and Earth, the youthful onesтАЭ makes the identity of тАЬthe two youthful onesтАЭ clear.

Geldner and Renou take y├бjadhyai as a predicated infinitive with unexpressed subject тАЬIтАЭ (without comment), with Agni the obj.: тАЬтАж Agni тАж will ich verehrenтАЭ; тАЬje veux lui sacrifier.тАЭ I instead supply тАЬ(I invoke)тАЭ (parallel to stuс╣г├й тАШI will praiseтАЩ in 1a) to govern agn├нm, who is then the subject of the inf. Although this involves supplying material, elsewhere in Agni contexts this infinitive is generally used of him, as subject, in his priestly role. Cf., e.g., III.1.1 тАж m─Б тАж v├бhniс╣Г cakartha vid├бthe y├бjadhyai тАЬyou have made me your draught-horse, to offer the sacrifice at the ritual distribution.тАЭ And in this hymn see VI.49.9 h├│t─Б yakс╣гat тАж agn├нс╕е тАЬthe Hotar Agni will sacrifice,тАЭ with Agni as agent-subject of the active verb.

Griffith

Him, to be praised at each tribe’s sacrifices, the Two young Matrons’ sober-minded Herald,
The Son of Strength, the Child of Heaven, the signal of sacrifice, red Agni will I worship.

Geldner

Den besonnenen Lenker der beiden jugendlichen Rodasi, bei den Opfern jedes Stammes anzurufen, Agni, das Kind des Himmels, den Sohn der Kraft, das Wahrzeichen des Opfers, den R├╢tlichen will ich verehren.

Grassmann

Der preisenswerth beim Opfer jedes Stammes den beiden Jungfraun dient bedachten Geistes, Des Himmels Spross, den Sohn der St├дrke, Agni, des Opfers rothe Fahne will ich ehren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the two daughters of the radiant (sun) of various form, of whom one glitters with stars, the other (is bright) with the sun, mutually opposed, proceeding diversely, purifying (all things), and entitled to our laudation, be plural ased by the praise they hear (from us).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The two daughters: day and night, the daughters of the sun, directly or their cause, indirectly

Jamison Brereton

The two daughters of the ruddy one, differing in form: the one is ornamented with stars, the other is the sunтАЩs.
The two pure ones, transiting alternately, wandering apartтАФbeing
hymned they both approach the prayerful thought once it is heard.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My tr. of s┼л╠Бro any─Б╠БтАЬthe other is the sunтАЩsтАЭ follows Oldenberg, who adopted it from Ludwig. Geldner (/Renou) supply an instr. ra┼Ыm├нbhiс╕е тАШwith the raysтАЩ, parallel to stс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е, on which s┼л╠Бraс╕е depends. This seems unnec. RenouтАЩs claim that the accent on pipi┼Ы├й тАЬd├йconseille lтАЩinterpretation de s┼л╠Бraс╕е donn├йe par OldenbergтАЭ does not convince: although by the Oldenberg reading pipi┼Ы├й is not part of both any─Б╠Бclauses as it would be with the additional instr., it occurs at the boundary of two explicitly contrastive clauses, which would, I think, be sufficient to induce accent.

Griffith

Unlike in form are the Red God’s two Daughters: one is the Sun’s, and stars bedeck the other.
Apart, the Sanctifiers, in succession, come to the famed hymn, praised in holy verses.

Geldner

Von verschiedenem Aussehen sind die beiden T├╢chter des R├╢tlichen: die eine ist mit den Sternen geschm├╝ckt, die andere mit den Strahlen des Sonnengottes Surya, die getrennt wandeln, sich gegenseitig einholend, die Reinen kommen besungen zu dem geh├╢rten Gebet.

Grassmann

Des feurigrothen ungleichfarb’ge T├╢chter, die eine sterngeschm├╝ckt, mit Licht die andre, In stetem Wechsel wandernd, herrlich prangend, besungen gehn sie zum geh├╢rten Liede.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay our earnest praise proceed to the presence of V─Бyu, the possessor of vast riches, the desired of all, the filler of his chariot (with wealth for his worshippers); most adorable (V─Бyu), who are riding in a radiant car, and driving your Niyut (steeds), do you, who are far-seeing, show favour to the sage, (your adorer).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Kavim iyakс╣гasi prayajyo: prayajyo is applied to the priest, the adhvaryu; worship, venerable priest, the wise V─Бyu…

Jamison Brereton

A lofty inspired thought (goes) forth to V─Бyu, who, possessing lofty wealth and all valuables, fills the chariot.
Having a brilliant course, master of teams, as poet you seek to reach the poet, you who are worshiped at the forefront of the sacrifice.

Griffith

I with a lofty song call hither Vayu, all-bounteous, filler of his car, most wealthy.
Thou, Sage, with bright path, Lord of harnessed horses, impetuous, promptly honourest the prudent.

Geldner

Mein hohes Sinnen geht zu Vayu dem Vielbegehrten mit hohem Reichtum und vollem Wagen. In gl├дnzender Auffahrt, die Niyut besitzend, begehrst du, der Seher, nach dem Seher, du Opfersamer.

Grassmann

Hin zu dem Vaju dring das grosse Preislied, der reich an allen G├╝tern vollen Wagens Im Glanze f├дhrt, mit Vielgespann versehen; als weiser ehrst den weisen du, o St├╝rmer.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that splendid car of the A┼Ыvins, which is harnessed at a thought, clothe my form (with radiance); that (car) with which, N─Бsaty─Бs, leaders of (rites), you go to the dwelling (of the worshipper) to fulfil his desires for his posterity and himself.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

That seems to me a wonderтАФthe chariot of the A┼Ыvins, radiant, yoked with mind,
by which you two, N─Бsatyas, superior men, drive your circuit, for our descendants and ourselves to prosper.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the tricky word positioning, with p─Бda-final y├бс╕е picking up p─Бda-init.

s├б, in a nominal rel. cl. continued in the next p─Бda. It may be that in a structurally simple hymn like this the poet seeks to vary the ways he introduces the listed divinities and their attributes and to jazz up the syntax.

Griffith

That chariot of the Asvins, fair to look on, pleaseth me well, yoked with a thought, refulgent,
Wherewith, Nasatyas, Chiefs, ye seek our dwelling, to give new strength to us and to our children.

Geldner

Wie ein Wunder deucht mir der gl├дnzende Wagen der Asvin, der sich auf blo├Яen Gedanken anschirrt, auf dem ihr Herren Nasatya eure Rundfahrt macht, um unserer Nachkommenschaft und uns selbst Labung zu spenden.

Grassmann

Der Wagen der A├зvinen d├╝nkt mich herrlich, der leuchtende, durch Geistes Macht geschirrte, Auf dem, o treue M├дnner, ihr zur St├дtte erscheint zu st├дrken uns und unsre Kinder.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬParjanya and V─Бta, showerers of rain, and from te firmament available waters; sage Maruts, hearers of the truth, establishers of the world, multiply the moveable (wealth of him) by whose praises (you are propitiated).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Multiply: jagad ─Бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam = jagat: fixed as well as moveable, all living things, jagat sth─Бvara jaс╣Еgam─Бtmakam sarvam pr─Бс╣Зij─Бtam

Jamison Brereton

Parjanya [/Thunder] and V─Бta [/Wind], you two bulls of the earth, quicken the watery outpourings (for him [=human poet])
through whose hymnsтАФyou poets who really hear [=Maruts] and you mounter of the moving world [=Indra]тАФyou made the moving world your own.

Jamison Brereton Notes

If my comment immed. above is correct, this vs. is a fine example of it. To begin with the surface, the first hemistich has a dual voc. (p├бrjanyav─Бt─Б) and a dual impv. (jinvatam). So far all is well. But the 2nd hemistich has a plural voc. (s├бtya┼Ыrutaс╕е kavayaс╕е), whose referents are not identified, and a singular voc. (j├бgata sth─Бtar), whose referent is not identified, flanking a rel. prn. in the gen. and an instr.

pl. (y├бsya g─лrbh├нс╕е), with the rest of the vs., following the singular voc., containing an apparent main cl. verb in the 2nd pl. (─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam [so Pp.]). The simplest thing to do is to disjoin the two half-verses, keeping the dual and plural parts separate. But that leaves us with an incomplete rel. cl. that has nothing to do. The problems are discussed at length by Oldenberg, though he does not come to a firm determination.

Both Geldner and Renou take the first hemistich as independent, as do Oldenberg and Scarlatta (556). By contrast, I consider it the main cl. on which cd is dependent. Since my interpr. of ab resembles theirs almost to the end, however, we are in happy agreement so far. For the connection of Parjanya and V─Бta with the p├║r─лс╣г─Бni тАж ├бpy─Бni тАЬwatery outpourings,тАЭ cf. X.65.9 parj├бny─Бv─Б╠Бt─Б vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б╠Бpur─лс╣г├нn─Б. The only question is whether pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е in our passage depends on vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б or the watery outpourings: its accent (as opposed to unaccented voc. vс╣Ыс╣гabh─Б) speaks (weakly: see Oldenberg comm.) for the latter, the p─Бda break for the former, and the consensus is for the former. IтАЩm not at all sure it matters.

In my interpr. of ab as the main cl. to cd, I supply a beneficial dat. тАЬfor him,тАЭ referring to the human poet, to serve as main cl. referent for the rel. y├бsya in c. As just noted, the standard interpr. take ab as an independent cl., and therefore must account for the rel. prn. y├бsya in a different way. Before tackling that, let us first determine who the vocc. in cd refer to.

The pl. voc. phrase s├бtya┼Ыrutaс╕е kavayaс╕е beginning p─Бda c: by almost universal agreement, beg. with S─Бyaс╣Зa., this refers to the Maruts, on the basis of the p─Бda-spanning voc. phrase s├бtya┼Ыrutaс╕е k├бvayaс╕е y├║v─Бnaс╕е used of the Maruts in V.57.8, the only other occurrences of satya-┼Ыrut-. (It is worth remarking here that, though in both V.57.8 and here the p─Бda opens with the first two vocc., in V.57.8 k├бvayaс╕е is accented, whereas here it is not. I have no explan.) The identification with the Maruts seems reasonable, though of course nothing about the phrase uniquely identifies the Maruts. However, note that in vs. 11 below they are addressed as yuv─Бnaс╕е kavayaс╕е, with two of the terms found in V.57.8.

As for j├бgata sth─Бtar in d, most tr. leave the referent unidentified (e.g., Geldner n.

6cd тАЬWer der j├бgataс╕е sth─Бtar sein soll, ist nicht deutlich.тАЭ). Since the agent noun sth─Б╠Бtar- in the sg. is otherwise used only of Indra, he seems a likely referent, esp.

because he is also regularly associated with the Maruts. The added wrinkle is that there must be a pun here as well: the stem sth─Бt├бr- (so accented) тАШthe stillтАЩ, always in the form sth─Бt├║с╕е, is the regular formulaic partner of j├бgat- тАШthe movingтАЩ; cf., e.g., in the next hymn, VI.50.7 v├н┼Ыvasya sth─Бt├║r j├бgataс╕е. The poetтАЩs urge to make this play on words may have contributed both to the contorted syntax and the unclarity of reference weтАЩre trying to untangle.

The two referents of the vocative phrases, the Maruts and (if IтАЩm right) Indra, are the joint 2nd pl. subjects of the verb in d. On this, I think, we are all agreed. But all standard interpr. follow the Pp. in taking ─Б╠З╠Бkс╣Ыnudhvam as an unaccented, and therefore main clause, verb. (See, explicitly, Oldenberg тАЬтАж ist offenbar Imperativ und hat Hauptsatzakzent.тАЭ) Under this interpr., something else has to be done with the y├бsya g─лrbh├нс╕е of c. Most people supply material like mad: Geldner adds a тАЬtowards himтАЭ in his main cl. and тАЬyou take pleasureтАЭ as verb in the rel. cl.: тАЬmachet alles was lebt, (dem) geneigt, an dessen Loblied (ihr Freude habt)тАЭ – in other words, he manufactures most of the relative cl.; Scarlatta similar, though he gives a wide choice of ways to fill out the rel. cl., thus demonstrating exactly how untethered this interpr. is: тАЬdurch dessen Lieder{ihr das k├╢nnt/ihr so heiss/ihr gepriesen werdet} (?).тАЭ Renou, by contrast, eliminates the rel. cl. by folding it into a voc.: тАЬ(toi) par les paroles de qui (les chose se r├йalisent)тАЭ – though it still requires extensive material to fill it out, again based on nothing.

My solution is to take ─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam as the verb of the rel. cl.: the Saс╣Гhit─Б text of course reads ─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam; it is only the Pp. that inserts a notional word space after ─Б╠Б. If we instead interpr. the sequence as an augmented imperfect, with accent on the augment, that is, ─Б + ├бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam (which does not require emendation), we do not have to fill out the rel. cl., because it already has an accented verb and that verb has an object: тАЬyou made the moving world your own.тАЭ This expression, ─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы (middle)

  • INSTR. has close parallels, one containing g─лrbh├нс╕е as here: cf. I.77.2 t├бm ┼л n├бmobhir ─Б╠Бkrс╣З╠е udhvam / X.6.5 agn├нс╣Г g─лrbh├нr n├бmobhir ─Б╠Бkrс╣З╠е udhvam. In both those passages I tr. тАЬattract here with reverence (and hymns).тАЭ The difference in interpr. may be ascribed to the fact that in our passage here, the gods are subj. and the hymns come from the human poet, whereas in the two passages just cited mortals are also the subj.

However, I may want to rethink both of those passages, to тАЬmake him [/Agni] your own.тАЭ Since in both passages Agni is the object, he does not have to be attracted here, since as the ritual fire he already is here.

Thus, by my interpr. all of cd is a rel. cl., dependent on a тАЬfor himтАЭ or the like to be supplied in the main cl. of ab. Note that both Geldner (тАЬdemтАЭ) and Scarlatta. (тАЬf├╝r ihnтАЭ) must supply the same beneficial dative, but they do so with the supposed main cl.

verb ─Б╠Бkс╣Ыс╣Зudhvam in d. Although my interpr. produces an awk English tr., it accounts for the Sanskrit considerably better than the alternatives. What it means for the gods to тАЬmake the moving world their ownтАЭ IтАЩm not sure – but perhaps the usual RVic notion that human praises strengthen the gods for their heroic deeds and, perhaps in this case, that these praises bring the gods and their human worshipers (part of the тАЬmoving worldтАЭ) into a closer relationship.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the purifying, amiable, graceful Sarasvat─л, the bride of the hero, favour our pious rite; may she, together with the wives of the gods, well plural ased, bestow upon him who praises her a habitation free from defects and impenetrable (to wind and rain), and (grant him) felicity.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amiable: kany─Б = a maiden (gn─Бс╕е g─Бyajy─Бd─лni chand─Бс╣Гsi, chand─Бс╣Гsi vai gn─Бс╕е: Taitir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 5.1.7.2); kaman─лy─Б, to be desired or loved;

V─лrapatn─л = the wife of the hero (Praj─Бpati or Brahm─Б); or, simply, the protectress of heroes or of men

Jamison Brereton

The daughter of Pav─лru, the maiden with a brilliant lifespan, Sarasvat─л, whose husband is a hero, will confer poetic insight.
Together with the (divine) ladies she will hold out to the singer unbroken shelter, protection difficult to assail.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the syntactic pyrotechnics of the previous vs., this one comes as a relief. Because of the subjunctive yaс╣Гsat ending the vs., I assume a modal value also for dh─Бt ending the first hemistich, as do Geldner and Renou

Griffith

So may Sarasvati, the Hero’s Consort, brisk with rare life, the lightning’s Child, inspire us,
And, with the Dames accordant, give the singer a refuge unassailable and flawless.

Geldner

Die Tochter des Paviru, das M├дdchen von wunderbarer Lebenskraft, die Sarasvati, die Heldeng├╢ttin m├╢ge guten Gedanken eingeben. Mit den G├╢tterfrauen vereint m├╢ge sie dichten Schirm, unantastbaren Schutz dem S├дnger gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Die lebensfrische Maid, die blitzerzeugte. Sarasvati erh├╢r, die Heldengattin, Vereint den Weibern reiche sichern Schutz sie, dem S├дnger Zuflucht, der kein Feind sich nahet.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay (the worshipper), influenced by the hope (of reward), approach with praise the adorable (P┼лс╣гan), protector of all path; may he bestow upon us cows with golden horns; may P┼лс╣гan bring to perfection our every rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Protector: pathaspathaс╕е paripatim: P┼лс╣гan is the lord of the paths

Jamison Brereton

I will direct my eloquence to the complete protector of every path. Prompted by desire, he has attained the chant.
He will bestow on us proliferating riches tipped with gold; he will cause every visionary thought to reach its goalтАФP┼лс╣гan.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With most (Grassmann, Geldner, Renou), the published translation takes the hapax p├бripati- as ultimately derived from тИЪp─Б тАШprotectтАЩ, not p├бti- тАШlordтАЩ. However, this analysis has grave formal problems not solved by RenouтАЩs cavalier тАЬhapax tir├й de p─Б- тАж mais influenc├й, pour la forme, par p├бtiтАЭ: it would be quite difficult to get a short-vowel root syllable pafrom тИЪp─Б by any normal derivational process. I now think that it is a cmpd. of -p├бti-, even though WackernagelтАЩs тАШringsum HerrтАЩ (AiG II.1.260) reflecting this analysis is not terribly satisfactory. My change of heart was occasioned by considering the first verse in the first hymn of the P┼лс╣гan cycle that begins soon after this hymn, VI.53.1, whose first p─Бda ends pathas pate тАЬo lord of the path.тАЭ I would now tr. our passage, тАЬthe complete lord of every path.тАЭ It might be worth noting that VI.53.1 also enlists P┼лс╣гanтАЩs help with our dh─л╠Б- тАШvisionary thoughtтАЩ, as here.

Most take vacasy─Б╠Бas instr. sg. to the -─Б╠Бstem vacasy─Б╠Б- тАШeloquenceтАЩ, requiring a verb to be supplied (e.g., Geldner тАЬ(preise ich)тАЭ). I instead interpr. it as 1st sg. act. to the denom. vacasya- (not otherwise found accented). There are two problems with my analysis: 1) the other two forms of the verb vacasya- are medial; 2) vacasy─Б╠Бis accented, though supposedly a main-cl. verb. The first is not too difficult: verbs of proclaiming/praising can be labile with regard to voice. The second is more problematic and might require me to follow the standard view, tr. тАЬ(I praise, vel sim.) with my eloquence.тАЭ But see disc. of vardh├бy─Б in 10b, where I suggest that our vacasy─Б╠Бhere is indeed a verb and has borrowed its verbal accent from vardh├бy─Б.

The phrase k─Б╠Бmena kс╣Ыt├бс╕е is used of P┼лс╣гan also in nearby VI.58.3-4.

Griffith

I praise with eloquence him who guards all pathways. He, when his love impelled him, went to Arka.
May he vouchsafe us gear with gold to grace it: may Pusan make each prayer of ours efective.

Keith

Lord of each way with eloquence;
Driven by love he went to Arka;
May he give us the comfort of gold,
May Pusan further our every prayer.

Geldner

Den H├╝ter eines jeden Weges preise ich mit Beredsamkeit. Der Verliebte hat den Preis gewonnen. Er schenke uns Belohnungen mit Gold an der Spitze. Jedes Gebet m├╢ge Pusan zum Ziel f├╝hren.

Grassmann

Zum H├╝ter jedes Weges drang das Loblied, das durch Begier aus Liederlust geschaffne; Er, Puschan, schenk uns glanzerf├╝llte Labung und m├╢ge jede Bitte uns erf├╝llen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the illustrious Agni, the invoker of the gods, worship (with this oblation), Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, the first divider (of forms), the renowned, the giver of food, the well-handed, the vast, the adored of householders, the readily invoked.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The adored: yajatam pasty─Бn─Бm: pastyam = house, and by metonymy used for householder, gс╣Ыhasthair yajan─лyam

Jamison Brereton

To him who receives the first portion, the glorious conferrer of vigor, the skillful god with lovely palms and lovely hands
who deserves the sacrifice of the dwelling placesтАФto Tvaс╣гс╣нar easy to invoke will far-radiant Agni, the Hotar, sacrifice.

Griffith

May Herald Agni, fulgent, bring for worship Tvastar adored, in homes and swift to listen,
Glorious, first to share, the life-bestower, the ever active God, fair-armed, fair-handed.

Geldner

Den Gott, dem der Vorrang geb├╝hrt, den angesehenen, kraftverleihenden, sch├╢nh├дndigen, sch├╢narmigen, geschickten soll der erstrahlende Agni, der Hotri, anbeten, den Angebeteten der H├дuser, den leicht zu errufenden Tvastri.

Grassmann

Dem sch├╢nen, der zuerst empf├дngt und Kraft gibt, dem Gott, der kunstvoll wirkt mit Arm und H├дnden, Dem opferreichen Tvaschtar opfre Agni, der H├дuser lichter Priester ihm, der gern h├╢rt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬExalt Rudra, the parent of the world, with these hmns by day; (exalt) Rudra (with them) by night; animated by the far-seeing, we invoke him, mighty, of plural asing aspect, undecaying, endowed with felicity, (the source of) prosperity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The father of creation: with these hymns strengthen Rudra by day, Rudra by night;
the lofty, high, ageless, very gracious one would we invoke separately, roused by the poet.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The form vardh├бy─Б can be either 2nd sg. impv. (Grassmann, Geldner) or 1st sg.

subjunctive (Renou). I opt for the latter, partly because there seem to be no other unambiguous impvs. addressed to priests/mortals in this hymn; the priestly/poetic function is represented by 1st sg. (e.g., stuс╣г├й 1a) and 1st pl. (e.g., huvema p─Бda d this vs.) verbs. It is also accented despite p─Бda-medial position, presumably because it lies in the center of a balanced construction: rudr├бс╣Г d├нv─Б тАж rudr├бm akta├║ тАЬRudra by day тАж Rudra by night.тАЭ Given this accented, non-initial, 1st sg. subj., I wonder if vacasy─Б╠Бin 8a is in fact also a verb (as in my first analysis, represented in the published

tr.) and has borrowed its accent from vardh├бy─Б.

Despite GeldnerтАЩ and RenouтАЩs comments, considering тАШseparatelyтАЩ (тАШalleinтАЩ, тАШ├а partтАЩ) for с╣Ы╠Бdhak only to reject it, this must be the correct tr. In his n. 10d Geldner cites II.33.4, where we hope not to anger Rudra by invoking him with an invocation shared with another god or gods. See comm. ad loc. The fact that RudraтАЩs sons are addressed in the next vs. (11), as well as namelessly in 6cd (see above), might make the need for a separate invocation of Rudra all the more acute.

Griffith

Rudra by day, Rudra at night we honour with these our songs, the Universe’s Father.
Him great and lofty, blissful, undecaying let us call specially as the Sage impels us.

Geldner

Rudra, den Vater der Welt, erbaue mit diesen Lobesworten bei Tag, Rudra in der Nacht! Den hohen, erhabenen, alterlosen, wohlwollenden Gott wollen wir recht anrufen, von dem Weisen angeregt.

Grassmann

Den Weltenvater st├дrk mit diesen Liedern am Tag den Rudra und bei Nacht den Rudra, Den hohen, grossen, ewig jungen, holden lasst rufen uns zusammt erregt vom Dichter.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬEver youthful wise, and adorable Maruts, come to the praise of your adorer; thus augmenting, leaders (of rites), and spreading (through the firmament), like rays (of light), refresh the scanty woods (with rain).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like rays of light: nakс╣гanto aс╣Еgirasvat = aс╣Еgirasaс╕е gamana┼Ы─лl─Бra┼Ыmayaс╕е, rays endowed with motions; te yatha ┼Ы─лghram nabhastalam vy─Бpnuvanti tad vat, as they spread quickly through the sky, so) do the winds; or, if aс╣Еgirasa is a reference to a с╣Ыс╣гi, the property of rapid movement is assigned to the с╣Ыс╣гis: yad va с╣Ыс╣гayastad vacch─лghrag─Бminaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

You youths, poets deserving the sacrifice, you MarutsтАФcome hither in response to the singerтАЩs longing for space,
for you in your strength quicken even (a place) without brightness,
approaching in just the same way as to Aс╣Еgiras, you superior men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The interpr. of varasy─Б╠Б- as somehow a deriv. of v├бra- тАШwishтАЩ, found, e.g., in Grassmann, Geldner, and AiG II.2.244, is contextually understandable: GeldnerтАЩs тАЬKommet тАж zum Bittgesuch des S├дngersтАЭ makes more immediate sense than my тАЬcome hither in response to the singer’s longing for space,тАЭ with тАЬin response toтАЭ smuggled in to make the sentence somewhat more parsable. But there is no v├бras- to тИЪvс╣Э тАШwish, chooseтАЩ, whereas v├бras- means тАШwide spaceтАЩ, something that RVic poets often express a desire for. Renou hesitates (his word), but opts for тАШdesire for spaceтАЩ and adduces the quite apposite I.181.9 varivasy─Б╠Бgс╣Ыс╣З─Бn├бс╕е тАЬsinging (to you) with a desire for space,тАЭ comparable to our gс╣Ыс╣Зat├│ varasy─Б╠Б.

The causal relationship between c and ab, suggested by h├н (c), is not straightforward. But in its only other occurrence (IV.51.3), acitr├б- refers to a place, one without brightness, therefore by implication sterile and lifeless. Thus the desire for (positive) space expressed in b is contrasted with (negative) space that the Maruts can, nonetheless, bring to life.

I donтАЩt understand the point of d.

Griffith

Ye who are youthful, wise, and meet for worship, come, Martits, to the longing of the singer.
Coming, as erst to Angiras, O Heroes, ye animate and quicken e’en the desert.

Geldner

Kommet, ihr jugendlichen, opferw├╝rdigen Seher, ihr Marut, zum Bittgesuch des S├дngers. Denn erstarkend belebt ihr auch das Unansehnliche, indem ihr hierher kommt wie zu den Angiras, ihr Herren.

Grassmann

Kommt her, o weise, jugendliche Maruts, ehrw├╝rd’ge ihr, auf das Begehr des S├дngers; Das Matte auch erquicket ihr belebend, o M├дnner, recht wie G├╢tterboten kommend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOffer adoration to the valiant, powerful, swift-movig (company of the Maruts), as the herdsman (drives his) herd to their stall; may that (company) appropriate to its own body the praises of the pious worshipper, as the firmament (is studded) with stars.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Forth to the hero, forth to the powerful, precipitous one will I drive (praise?), as a guardian of livestock drives his flocks home.
He will make the inspired words of the speaker touch the body of him who is famed, as one makes the firmament touched by stars.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. contains two exx. of case disharmony between simile and frame, one each in ab and cd.

Though Grassmann takes ├бj─Б as a 2nd sg. impv., both Geldner and Renou interpr. it as a 1st sg.

subjunctive, as do I. This would bring the count to three in this hymn, by my interpr.

(8a, 10b, 12b).

This verb takes a straightforward acc. obj. y┼лth─Б╠БтАШherdsтАЩ in the simile, as well as an adverbial acc. goal ├бstam тАШhomeтАЩ. But in the frame it lacks an overt obj.: I supply тАШpraiseтАЩ, Geldner тАШLiedтАЩ, Renou тАШmon hymneтАЩ. And the goal is the personal dative of the divinity (v─лr─Б╠Бya, etc.).

The mismatch between simile and frame is greater in cd, and once again the simile is the more straighforwardly expressed. The poet exploits the syntactic ambiguity of intrans./trans. -├бya- formations, in the form here of the redupl. aor.

pispс╣Ыsati тИЪspс╣Ы┼Ы тАШtouchтАЩ, meaning both тАШmake X [acc.] touch Y [acc./loc.]тАЩ and, notionally passive, тАШmake Y [acc.] touched by X [instr.]тАЩ. The simile uses the latter construction: тАЬcause the firmament (acc. n─Б╠Бkam = Y) to be touched by stars (instr.

stс╣Ы╠Бbhiс╕е =X). In the frame the X is the тАЬinspired wordsтАЭ (v├нpaс╕е, acc. pl.) and the Y is the body (tanv├м, in the loc., an alternative case to the acc. in this construction). Both words and body are limited by genitives, referring to the poet (vacan├бsya тАШof the speakerтАЩ) and the god (┼Ыrut├бsya тАШof the famed oneтАЩ). For further disc. of the passage and of the phenomenon in general see my тАЬCase Disharmony.тАЭ Our poet further muddies the waters by reversing the more common relationship between forms of тИЪvip and тИЪvac. The stem vacan├б- тАШspeaking, speakerтАЩ, referring to a person, is attested only 3x in the RV, whereas v├бcas- тАШspeechтАЩ is ubiquitous; the root noun v├нp- тАШinspired (word[s])тАЩ is not uncommon, but is far outnumbered by the stem v├нpra- тАШinspired poetтАЩ. So we might have expected the phrase *v├нprasya v├бcaс╕е тАЬthe speech of the inspired poetтАЭ (cf., though not with a gen., VIII.61.9 v├нpraс╕е тАж v├бcaс╕е), not vacan├бsya v├нpaс╕е тАЬthe inspired words of the speaker.тАЭ

Griffith

Even as the herdsman driveth home his cattle, I urge my songs to him the strong swift Hero
May he, the glorious, lay upon his body the singer’s hymns, as stars bedeck the heaven.

Geldner

Dem starken, ├╝berlegenen Manne will ich das Lied zutreiben wie der Hirt seine Herde heimtreibt. Er lasse die Reden des beredten S├дngers seinen, des Ber├╝hmten, Leib schm├╝cken wie den Himmel mit Sternen.

Grassmann

Ich treibe hin zum raschen, starken Helden die Lieder, wie zum Stall der Hirt die Heerden; Des S├дngers Lieder hefte der ber├╝hmte an seinen Leib wie Sterne an den Himmel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we be happy in a home, in riches, in person nn, in children, bestowd upon us by you, Viс╣гс╣Зu, who with three (steps) made the terrestrial reions for Manu when harassed (by the asuras).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He who measured out the earthly realms three times exactly, for Manu, who was hard-pressedтАФViс╣гс╣ЗuтАФ
in this shelter of yours (still) being offered might we rejoice with wealth, with life and lineage.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another syntactic trick, though far less complex than in the last vs. The first half-vs., describing Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs cosmogonic deed, is couched in the 3rd ps., with the pf. vimam├й тАШhe measured outтАЩ, but in the 2nd half, expressing our present-day desire to live under Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs protection, the god is in the more intimate 2nd ps., in the phrase t├бsya te, lit. тАЬof this you,тАЭ where t├бsya provides the syntactic pivot to 2nd sg. enclitic te. On such doublings see my тАЬsa fig├й.тАЭ For тАЬhard-pressed ManuтАЭ (m├бnave b─Бdhit─Б╠Бya), see the same phrase in VII.91.1, where, as here, a god (or gods) perform(s) a cosmogonic deed that allows the sacrifice to be instituted.

Griffith

He who for man’s behoof in his afiliction thrice measured out the earthly regions, Visnu-
When one so great as thou affordeth shelter, may we with wealth and with ourselves be happy.

Geldner

Nachdem Vishnu die irdischen R├дume dreimal durchmessen hat f├╝r den bedr├дngten Mann, wollen wir in deiner dargebotenen Zuflucht am Reichtum uns erg├╢tzen, wir selbst mit den Kindern.

Grassmann

Der dreimal auch der Erde R├дume ausschritt zum Nutzen des bedr├дngten Menschen, Vischnu, In dessen Schutze m├╢gen wir gedeihen, den du uns reichst, an Reichthum, Leib und Kindern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Ahirbudhnya (propitiated) by (our) hymns, and Parvata and Savit─Б give us food with water; may the bountiful (gods supply us), addition, with vegetable (grains); and may the all-wise Bhaga be propitious (to us) for (the acquisition of) riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ahirbudhnya: budhna = antarikс╣гa, firmament;

Budhnya = what or who is there born;

Ahi = he who goes, i.e., in the sky;

Parvata: the filler, p┼лrayitr─л, or the wielder of the thunderbolt, parvavad-vajram tadv─Бn; or, enemy of the mountain, gireс╕е ┼Ыatru; in either sense, the reference is to Indra; with vegetable grains: tad oс╣гadhibhir abhi = oс╣гadhayas tila m─Бс╣г─Бdayaс╕е, the vegetables are sesamum, pulse and the like

Jamison Brereton

Let Ahi Budhnya take delight in this (praise?) of ours, along with the waters and the chants; in this let the Mountain, in this let Savitar
take delight;
let the Gift-Escorts, let Fortune, let Plenitude quicken this along with the plants, for wealth.

Griffith

Sweet be this song of mine to Ahibudhnya, Parvata, Savitar, with Floods and Lightnings;
Sweet, with the Plants, to Gods who seek oblations. May liberal Bhaga speed us on to riches.

Geldner

Dies unser Lied nehm an der Wetterdrache, der Berg und Savitar nebst Wassern, Blitzen, Dies nebst den Kr├дutern auch die Gabenspender, Bhaga, Purandhi f├╢rdre uns zu Reichthum.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGrant us, (universal gods), riches, comprehending chariots, numerous dependants, many male offspring, (wealth) the giver of efficiency to the solemn rite, and a dwelling free from decay, wherewith we may overcome malevolent men and unrighteous (spirits), and afford support to those people who are devoted to the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now to us give wealth in chariots, filling the settled domains, consisting of many heroes, the herdsmen of great truth;
give ageless peaceful dwelling (and that) with which we will trample upon the (other) peoples, the godless contenders,
with which we will take on the godless clans.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation should read тАЬthe herdsman of great truth,тАЭ since gop─Б╠Бm modifies ray├нm.

With Oldenberg I read cakr├бm─Бma, a pf. subj., not ca kr├бm─Бma, pace Klein (DGRV I.188, 190). This reading is accepted by K├╝mmel (147 and n. 146).

I take kс╣г├бyam тАж y├йna тАж abh├н cakr├бm─Бma as an explicit тАЬX and (which) YтАЭ construction on grounds of content: I do not think our тАЬpeaceful dwellingтАЭ (kс╣г├бyam) is the means by which we will trample and destroy our enemies. Instead I think we have the usual RVic implicit contrast between war and peace (yoga-kс╣гem├б- in one rendition), with тАШpeaceтАЩ expressed by a noun and war by an elaborate rel. cl.

Griffith

Give riches borne on cars, with many heroes, contenting men, the guard of mighty Order.
Give us a lasting home that we may battle with godless bands of men who fight against us, and meet with tribes to whom the Gods are gracious.
